## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting stress (sigma) from strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in solid mechanics and materials science. The relationship captures how materials deform under load at different temperatures, involving elastic, plastic, and thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': "Hooke's law (temperature-dependent)", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * T) * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent elastic modulus'}

- {'name': 'Voce hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)', 'scenario': 'Saturation-type hardening approaching a limiting stress'}
- {'name': 'Johnson-Cook simplified (no strain rate)', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T**c4)', 'scenario': 'Coupled strain hardening and thermal softening for metals'}
- {'name': 'Linear thermal softening with hardening', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)', 'scenario': 'Power-law hardening modulated by linear temperature dependence'}
- {'name': 'Thermally-activated flow stress', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2', 'scenario': 'Power-law coupling between strain and temperature'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain with temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T', 'scenario': 'Second-order polynomial expansion including cross-terms'}
- {'name': 'Rubber elasticity (neo-Hookean type)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * epsilon**3)', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear elasticity for polymeric/rubber materials with entropic elasticity'}
- {'name': 'Exponential softening with strain', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Saturation hardening combined with thermal activation'}
- {'name': 'Swift hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2', 'scenario': 'Generalized power-law hardening with pre-strain offset'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c2*T) scaling the stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational epsilon/(epsilon + c) forms
- Thermal softening at high T → Homologous temperature factor (1 - (T*c0)**c1) or inverse T dependence
- Elastic-plastic transition → Additive decomposition: linear term c0*epsilon plus nonlinear hardening term
- Entropic elasticity in polymers → Stress proportional to T (sigma ~ c0*T*f(epsilon)), reflecting rubber elasticity
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicating thermomechanical interaction
- Concave-up then concave-down stress-strain → Cubic or higher-order polynomial in epsilon, or tanh-based forms
- Yield plateau behavior → Piecewise or smooth transition: c0*tanh(c1*epsilon) approximating elastic-perfectly-plastic response
